<review>Employees become increasingly annoying as I continue to come in.
My first visit, the bagger put tape all around his face and snickered as people gave him odd looks. It wasn't funny or endearing, just unprofessional.
My second visit I waited at the meat counter for a few minutes for someone to come out. When I finally went to find someone and they called him over the intercom, he busted out of the back yelling about his fellow employee. I informed him that we were waiting and he shot back "Yeah? For what? A minute?" Which sure, maybe it was a minute and I was eager to get my food and leave, who wouldn't with service like that.
My third visit, it was closing and the same man from the meat department was behind me in line, standing waaay too close for comfort because he wanted the cashier to ring out his bananas before he left, while simultaneously the manager asked the cashier across to take out the trash, to which he look at his customer, scoffed, and replied "Um, no."
On top of that, the bagger with the taped up face, thinks it's funny to ask every customer if they want cigarettes, and continues to push the idea upon them even after denying the offer. Again, not cute.

Crappy staff aside, they have what you need. But so does every other grocery store, which is why I won't be taking my buisness to this Albertsons again. The employees are too weird, and I never thought I'd have that strong an opinion about a grocery store.</review></record></dataset><record>

<pictures>None<//pictures>< Text>
Not worth it, overpriced and you can get better tacos from the taco truck a few blocks down for less.

The batter was burnt, and the overly sweet sauce they covered it with made it seem like I was eating a jelly doughnut wrapped in a tortilla.

Tacos are not meant to be sweet... For the love of everything holy, my hands are not supposed to be sticky after eating a taco!

I never thought you could mess up something so simple; the "unique" approach that they took to Mexican cuisine has made a mockery of it. It makes you question what person in their right mind greenlit the menu and thought Mexican food was missing turmeric rice and kale. I can honestly say I've had better Mexican food in West Virginia.

If you want overly priced food that will look pretty for your social media account, by all means, this is the place add a filter and watch the colors pop.

If you want savory food that isn't going to send you into diabetic shock, find a taco truck next to a construction site and enjoy some flavor.</Text>

<username>marc krigel<//username><date>1571696406350< /date><Rating>5<//Rating>< Review>
I just rediscovered this little stand on Westwood Blvd, a block and a half south of Santa Monica Blvd, on the west side of the street.
What a delicious find!
I had the Crispy Shrimp Bowl, with all kale (as opposed to rice, or half-and-half of each).
The shrimp was perfectly done and plentiful, the kale crisp and dark, black bean paste, corn, and a side of hot sauce the perfect complement.

Parking is problematic, but for a dollar or 2, the adjoining lot is well worth it.</Review>

<date>1577198725298<//date><rating>4< /rating>< Text>
We made a stop here for a quick, mildly cheap dinner, and we were thoroughly impressed by the quality of the tacos. They are a little more expensive than thought: if you're looking at the old menus, just know that the grilled and fried versions cost differently. The place had a very cute dining area with Spanish music playing, and we got our tacos fairly quickly. I was left quite full after two tacos, but managed to squeeze in a bite of the red velvet churros, which were pretty good. I wasn't expecting to detect that much of a difference between a normal churro and these flavored once, but I think they really nailed them! Definitely would recommend to friends near the UCLA area.</Text>

< user_name>
Jeanne Hart</user_name>
<Date>1493247087491<//Date>< Review>
Went to Tacos Tu Madre last night for Taco Tuesday. They have a nice menu of gourmet tacos which includes some Korean flavors. I ordered their Spicy Citrus Carnitas and Grilled Chicken Tacos. They both had good flavors, especially the carnitas, but unfortunately both tacos were lukewarm, on the side of cold, from the first bite. The two others in my group (one ordered tacos, the other a bowl) had the same issue. It was also about a 15-20 minute wait after ordering. I wouldn't mind the wait if they were super busy, but there were only three tickets ahead of us and I can't remember ever waiting that long at a food truck or any other taco stand. All in all, it was okay, but with so many other taco options in Los Angeles, I can't say I would return right away.< /Review>

Well, coming from the Happy Wife / Happy Life school of matrimony, I obeyed. I mean it was the last thing on Earth I felt like but.........

Taco's Tu Madre looked like it would fit comfortably in Tijuana, Mexico City or just about any Pueblo south of the border. The only difference was there was a lot of people waiting to order. < text>
Walk up taco window with very, very limited seating. Inside seats maybe 12, snugly. They told us it would take 30 minutes for our food...4 tacos. It came faster, but good lord, how hard is it to make 4 tacos. It wasn't that packed, so maybe the bulk of their business is to go and deliveries.

The tacos are on the smallish side for the price. $4-$6 for a two bite taco. But the flavors were very good. I tried the KBBQ and carne asada, while my friend had the fried avocado and something vegan. He loved the fried avocado, which I would like to go back and try.

Parking on Westwood is a nightmare, so may the forces be with you.

Bonus: tasty tacos
Bogus: no restrooms, westside prices

Will I be back? Sure, why not...but I'm not itching to return immediately.</text>

<review>Went here in late August, 2018 and was really disappointed in what's happened to this place.

- Prices went up
- Food quality declined
- The already long wait got longer

They had the best burritos and tacos in Westwood (some of the best in all of West LA), and I'm assuming they're under new management, as the decline in their quality and rise in their prices links up perfectly with them giving this place an unnecessary facelift (a couple neon signs, some window decals, and some signage plugging their social media). The wait had never been great here, but I always chalked that up to the undersized kitchen they're working with, and it was more than made up for by how good the food was. Now, the wait is significantly longer (there were multiple customers who had to check in to make sure their food was still coming out) for drastically worse food, at a higher price.

Really bummed to see them focus on changing things that didn't need to be changed and sacrificing what made this place great in the process.</review><user_name>Jordan Spratt</user_name></record></dataset><record>

<date>1452382095173</date><Gmap_id>0x80c2bb9c69a8d893:0x7ba8cea58a74bd57</Gmap_id><pics>None<//pics><Name>Steven Vong</Name><Response>None<//Response>< Text>
Bella Pita has been converted to a hip new taco stand with contemporary taco combinations. They have standard asada, pollo, but also fish and even duck. I came here from brunch and thought the tacos were just average and too small to justify the price.

I tried the egg and chorizo taco, as well as a chicken and guacamole. The presentation was okay, but the food itself was underwhelming. I think the meat from both tacos could have fit on a single tablespoon. The flavors were ok, but I was left unsatisfied with two tacos.

I also ordered red velvet churros for dessert, and they were better than the tacos. It came in 5 bite sized pieces with cream cheese filling and whipped cream.

Although they attempt to be hip and new, a taco is best when its simpler- and I'd rather have it from a truck or an establishment where they have perfected a few simple taco items.</Text>
